Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is caused by the obstruction of the upper airway during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cysts are odontogenic cysts that develop in the jawbones and do not cause upper airway obstruction.
  Orbital fracture is a fracture of the bones surrounding the eye and does not cause upper airway obstruction.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition that causes stiffness of the jaw joint, which can lead to difficulty in opening the mouth, but it does not cause upper airway obstruction.
  Therefore, none of the given options cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where the airway is partially or completely blocked during sleep, leading to breathing difficulties.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are benign tumors that can cause swelling and pain in the jaw, but they do not typically cause airway obstruction.
  Orbital fracture is a break in the bones surrounding the eye, which can cause double vision, but it does not typically cause airway obstruction.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joints are fused, which can restrict jaw movement and cause difficulty opening the mouth, but it can also cause airway obstruction.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:

  The floor of the third ventricle is a thin, diamond-shaped region.
  It is formed by the hypothalamus and the optic chiasm.
  The mammillary bodies are located posteriorly to the hypothalamus.
  The optic stalk and the infundibulum are located anteriorly to the hypothalamus.
  The third nerve is located laterally to the hypothalamus.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the Mammillary body.

Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in

Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young

  Pulp capping is a dental procedure that involves placing a medicament over an exposed pulp to encourage the formation of secondary dentin.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in a child's mouth.
  Primary teeth have a wider pulp chamber and a thinner dentin layer than permanent teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young is a characteristic of primary teeth.
  Odontoblasts are cells that produce dentin.
  Therefore, pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth because of increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
  The answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.

  Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth may not be a factor in the success of these procedures.

Choices:

  C: A>D>B>C

  The auditory cortex is the final destination of the auditory pathway.
  Therefore, the correct sequence from peripheral to central is: Cochlear nucleus > Inferior colliculus > Medial geniculate body > Auditory cortex.
  The answer is B: B>D>C>A.

  The inferior colliculus sends signals to the medial geniculate body.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a type of periodontal surgery.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means the roots of the tooth have been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL (Periodontal Ligament) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  Cementum is a layer of hard, mineralized tissue that covers the roots of teeth.
  Dentin is a hard, dense, bony tissue that forms the bulk of the tooth.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the body.
  Co adaptation refers to the ability of tissues to adapt to each other.
  Based on the choices, the most likely answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used to access the root surface of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibers are attached to the cementum and alveolar bone.
  If the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibers have been lost or destroyed.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

Question: Looseness seen in a recently delivered RPD is due to:
Choices:
  A: Defective occlusal balancing
  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:

  Looseness in RPD can be due to a variety of reasons.
  Passive clasp on abutment means the clasp is not engaging the abutment tooth properly.
  Defective occlusal balancing means the RPD is not fitting properly due to occlusal issues.
  Thin flange means the part of the RPD that contacts the gums is too thin.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means the RPD is not fitting properly due to the lack of overlap on posterior teeth.

Choices:

  B: Afferent arterioles of the glomeruli
  C: Thirst center in the hypothalamus
  D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus

ADH acts on the kidneys to increase water reabsorption.
The distal tubules and collecting ducts of the kidneys are responsible for water reabsorption.
Therefore, the primary site of action of antidiuretic hormone is on the distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.
The answer is A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.

Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a condition caused by excessive growth hormone (GH) production.
  GH is produced by the pituitary gland.
  Acromegaly is characterized by the enlargement of hands, feet, and facial bones.
  A large tongue may be a feature of acromegaly due to the enlargement of facial bones.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, which is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly, but hyperglycemia may occur due to insulin resistance.
  Crowded teeth may be a feature of acromegaly due to the enlargement of the jaw.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.

  The symptoms of acromegaly develop slowly over time.
  Some of the features of acromegaly include enlarged hands and feet, thickening of the skin, and coarsening of facial features.
  A large tongue is a feature of acromegaly due to the enlargement of the soft tissues of the mouth and throat.

  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.

Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piaget’s theory
Choices:

  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage

  The Sensorimotor stage is the first stage of Piaget's theory, which occurs from birth to around two years of age.
  During this stage, infants learn about the world through their senses and actions.

  Therefore, the answer is A: Sensorimotor.

Question: There is a swelling in a patient with respect to maxillary LI region, since last 48 hours, the swelling is hot & palpable & rebounds on pressure, the treatment of choice is
Choices:
  A: Incision & drainage
  B: Antibiotic coverage
  C: Antibiotics of heat only
  D: Aspiration
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has a swelling in the maxillary LI region that is hot and palpable.
  The swelling rebounds on pressure, which indicates that it is an abscess.
  The treatment of choice for an abscess is incision and drainage.
  Antibiotics alone will not be effective in treating an abscess.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Proteinuria, or the presence of excess protein in the urine, is a common sign of preeclampsia.
  Severe preeclampsia is diagnosed when there is a systolic blood pressure of 160 mmHg or higher, or a diastolic blood pressure of 110 mmHg or higher, along with other signs and symptoms.
  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists, severe proteinuria is defined as 5 grams or more of protein in a 24-hour urine collection or a urine protein-creatinine ratio of 0.5 or higher.
  None of the answer choices match the definition of severe proteinuria for preeclampsia.
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, most often the liver and kidneys.
  Proteinuria is the presence of excess protein in the urine and is one of the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
  Severe preeclampsia is a more severe form of preeclampsia.
  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists (ACOG), severe preeclampsia is defined as having a blood pressure of 160/110 mmHg or higher on two occasions, at least 4 hours apart, and one or more of the following: proteinuria of 5 g or more in a 24-hour urine specimen or 3+ or greater on two random urine samples collected at least 4 hours apart.
  5 g is equal to 5000 mg, and 3+ is equal to 300 mg or more.
  Therefore, the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is 300 mg or more.

Question: A 9 year old boy presenting with lytic lesion on midshaft tibia. On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Xray is as shown below. What is the likely diagnosis?
Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lytic lesion in the midshaft of the tibia in a 9-year-old boy is a common presentation of a bone tumor.
  The HPE findings of grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm, and fibroblastic proliferation are characteristic of a giant cell tumor.
  The X-ray shows an eccentric lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion, which is also typical of a giant cell tumor.
  Therefore, the likely diagnosis is B: Giant cell tumor.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The clinical presentation describes a lytic lesion on midshaft tibia in a 9-year-old boy.
  The histopathological findings include grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm, and fibroblastic proliferation.
  The X-ray shows an eccentric, lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion.
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis, also known as eosinophilic granuloma, is a rare condition that affects children and young adults. It is characterized by the proliferation of Langerhans cells, which are a type of dendritic cell. The histopathological findings in Langerhans cell histiocytosis include the presence of Langerhans cells, eosinophils, and giant cells. The X-ray findings may include lytic lesions with cortical thinning and expansion.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign tumor that typically affects the epiphysis of long bones in adults. The histopathological findings include the presence of multinucleated giant cells, spindle-shaped stromal cells, and hemosiderin-laden macrophages. The X-ray findings may include an eccentric, lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare, benign tumor that typically affects the epiphysis of long bones in children and young adults. The histopathological findings include the presence of chondroblasts, which are large, round cells with abundant cytoplasm and a central nucleus. The X-ray findings may include a well-defined, eccentric, lytic lesion with sclerotic margins.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign tumor that typically affects the cortex of long bones in children and young adults. The histopathological findings include the presence of osteoid, which is unmineralized bone matrix, and osteoblasts, which are cells that produce bone. The X-ray findings may include a well-defined, eccentric, lytic lesion with a central nidus and surrounding sclerosis.
  Based on the clinical presentation, histopathological findings, and X-ray findings, the most likely diagnosis is Giant cell tumor.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be cautious about drug usage as drugs can be secreted in the milk and affect the baby.
  Some drugs can be secreted negligibly in the milk, but others can be harmful to the baby.
  Longer half-life drugs can accumulate in the milk and affect the baby.
  Feeding the baby just before the next dose can reduce the amount of drug in the milk.
  It is not advisable to stop feeding the baby as breast milk is important for the baby's growth and development.
  Therefore, the best option is to advise the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Drugs taken by a lactating mother can be secreted into the breast milk and can affect the baby.
  The amount of drug secreted in the milk depends on the drug's properties, such as molecular weight, lipid solubility, and protein binding.
  The half-life of the drug determines the time taken for the drug to be eliminated from the body.
  Feeding the baby just before the next dose can help reduce the amount of drug in the milk.
  Withholding feeding is not recommended as it can lead to decreased milk production and affect the baby's growth.
  Therefore, the correct answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.

Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is responsible for the synthesis of heme, which is an important component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  The accumulation of which substance in blood reflects the inhibition of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway?
  Uroporphyrinogen III, Porphobinogen I, and Delta amino levulinic acid are intermediates of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  The accumulation of Delta amino levulinic acid in blood is a characteristic feature of lead poisoning.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is responsible for the synthesis of heme, which is a component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  The accumulation of what substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  Uroporphyrinogen III and Coproporphyrinogen III are intermediates in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Ferrochelatase is the final enzyme in the pathway that incorporates iron into protoporphyrin IX to form heme.
  Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first intermediate in the pathway.
  Porphobinogen is a precursor of heme and is formed from the condensation of four molecules of ALA.
  Therefore, the accumulation of Porphobinogen in blood reflects the inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway in lead poisoning.

Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease, which means the kidneys are functioning at less than 15% of normal capacity.
  The patient has Type 2 diabetes mellitus and doesn't want to take injectable insulin.
  The patient's renal function is severely impaired, which means the choice of oral hypoglycemic agents will be limited.
  Linagliptin, Vildagliptin, and Repaglinide are non-sulfonylurea secretagogues and do not require renal dose adjustment.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea and requires renal dose adjustment.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be either Linagliptin, Vildagliptin, or Repaglinide.
  Among the given options, only A: Linagliptin, and C: Vildagliptin are non-sulfonylurea secretagogues.
  Therefore, the answer is either A: Linagliptin or C: Vildagliptin.

  Glimepiride is metabolized in the liver and excreted in the urine, so it requires renal dose adjustment.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be either A: Linagliptin or C: Vildagliptin, or B: Repaglinide.

Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every nth element is selected from a list or sequence.
  Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every individual has an equal chance of being selected.
  Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into subgroups and individuals are randomly selected from each subgroup.
  Cluster sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into clusters and a random sample of clusters is selected.
  The question is asking about a sampling method that selects patients based on potential factors that will affect the results.
  This sounds like stratified random sampling, where the population is divided into subgroups based on potential factors and individuals are randomly selected from each subgroup.

  Calcium and vitamin D supplements are important for the development of strong bones and teeth in the baby, but there is no evidence that they increase birth weight.
  Bed rest is recommended in certain high-risk pregnancies, but there is no evidence that it increases birth weight.
  Therefore, cessation of smoking is the only option that can increase birth weight.
Action: Answer("A")
